<h3 id="Saving-Variables-with-the-shelve-Module">Saving Variables with the shelve Module</h3>
<p>To save variables:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> shelve

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>cats = [<span class="hljs-string">'Zophie'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'Pooka'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'Simon'</span>]
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">with</span> shelve.open(<span class="hljs-string">'mydata'</span>) <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> shelf_file:
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    shelf_file[<span class="hljs-string">'cats'</span>] = cats
</code></pre>
<p>To open and read variables:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">with</span> shelve.open(<span class="hljs-string">'mydata'</span>) <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> shelf_file:
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    print(type(shelf_file))
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    print(shelf_file[<span class="hljs-string">'cats'</span>])
&lt;<span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> '<span class="hljs-title">shelve</span>.<span class="hljs-title">DbfilenameShelf</span>'&gt;
['<span class="hljs-title">Zophie</span>', '<span class="hljs-title">Pooka</span>', '<span class="hljs-title">Simon</span>']
</span></code></pre>
<p>Just like dictionaries, shelf values have keys() and values() methods that will return list-like values of the keys and values in the shelf. Since these methods return list-like values instead of true lists, you should pass them to the list() function to get them in list form.</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">with</span> shelve.open(<span class="hljs-string">'mydata'</span>) <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> shelf_file:
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    print(list(shelf_file.keys()))
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    print(list(shelf_file.values()))
[<span class="hljs-string">'cats'</span>]
[[<span class="hljs-string">'Zophie'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'Pooka'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'Simon'</span>]]
</code></pre>
<h3 id="Saving-Variables-with-the-pprint.pformat()-Function">Saving Variables with the pprint.pformat() Function</h3>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> pprint

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>cats = [{<span class="hljs-string">'name'</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'Zophie'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'desc'</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'chubby'</span>}, {<span class="hljs-string">'name'</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'Pooka'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'desc'</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'fluffy'</span>}]

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>pprint.pformat(cats)
<span class="hljs-string">"[{'desc': 'chubby', 'name': 'Zophie'}, {'desc': 'fluffy', 'name': 'Pooka'}]"</span>

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">with</span> open(<span class="hljs-string">'myCats.py'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'w'</span>) <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> file_obj:
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    file_obj.write(<span class="hljs-string">'cats = {}\n'</span>.format(pprint.pformat(cats)))
<span class="hljs-number">83</span>
</code></pre>
<h3 id="Reading-ZIP-Files">Reading ZIP Files</h3>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> zipfile, os

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>os.chdir(<span class="hljs-string">'C:\\'</span>)    <span class="hljs-comment"># move to the folder with example.zip</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">with</span> zipfile.ZipFile(<span class="hljs-string">'example.zip'</span>) <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> example_zip:
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    print(example_zip.namelist())
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    spam_info = example_zip.getinfo(<span class="hljs-string">'spam.txt'</span>)
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    print(spam_info.file_size)
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    print(spam_info.compress_size)
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    print(<span class="hljs-string">'Compressed file is %sx smaller!'</span> % (round(spam_info.file_size / spam_info.compress_size, <span class="hljs-number">2</span>)))

[<span class="hljs-string">'spam.txt'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'cats/'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'cats/catnames.txt'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'cats/zophie.jpg'</span>]
<span class="hljs-number">13908</span>
<span class="hljs-number">3828</span>
<span class="hljs-string">'Compressed file is 3.63x smaller!'</span>
</code></pre>
<h3 id="Extracting-from-ZIP-Files">Extracting from ZIP Files</h3>
<p>The extractall() method for ZipFile objects extracts all the files and folders from a ZIP file into the current working directory.</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> zipfile, os

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>os.chdir(<span class="hljs-string">'C:\\'</span>)    <span class="hljs-comment"># move to the folder with example.zip</span>

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">with</span> zipfile.ZipFile(<span class="hljs-string">'example.zip'</span>) <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> example_zip:
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    example_zip.extractall()
</code></pre>
<p>The extract() method for ZipFile objects will extract a single file from the ZIP file. Continue the interactive shell example:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">with</span> zipfile.ZipFile(<span class="hljs-string">'example.zip'</span>) <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> example_zip:
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    print(example_zip.extract(<span class="hljs-string">'spam.txt'</span>))
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    print(example_zip.extract(<span class="hljs-string">'spam.txt'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'C:\\some\\new\\folders'</span>))
<span class="hljs-string">'C:\\spam.txt'</span>
<span class="hljs-string">'C:\\some\\new\\folders\\spam.txt'</span>
</code></pre>
<h3 id="Creating-and-Adding-to-ZIP-Files">Creating and Adding to ZIP Files</h3>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> zipfile

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">with</span> zipfile.ZipFile(<span class="hljs-string">'new.zip'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'w'</span>) <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> new_zip:
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    new_zip.write(<span class="hljs-string">'spam.txt'</span>, compress_type=zipfile.ZIP_DEFLATED)
</code></pre>
<p>This code will create a new ZIP file named new.zip that has the compressed contents of spam.txt.</p>
<h2 id="JSON,-YAML-and-configuration-files">JSON, YAML and configuration files</h2>
<h3 id="JSON">JSON</h3>
<p>Open a JSON file with:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> json
<span class="hljs-keyword">with</span> open(<span class="hljs-string">"filename.json"</span>, <span class="hljs-string">"r"</span>) <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> f:
    content = json.loads(f.read())
</code></pre>
<p>Write a JSON file with:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> json

content = {<span class="hljs-string">"name"</span>: <span class="hljs-string">"Joe"</span>, <span class="hljs-string">"age"</span>: <span class="hljs-number">20</span>}
<span class="hljs-keyword">with</span> open(<span class="hljs-string">"filename.json"</span>, <span class="hljs-string">"w"</span>) <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> f:
    f.write(json.dumps(content, indent=<span class="hljs-number">2</span>))
</code></pre>
<h3 id="YAML">YAML</h3>
<p>Compared to JSON, YAML allows for much better human maintainability and gives you the option to add comments.
It is a convenient choice for configuration files where humans will have to edit it.</p>
<p>There are two main libraries allowing to access to YAML files:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="https://pypi.python.org/pypi/PyYAML">PyYaml</a></li>
<li><a href="https://pypi.python.org/pypi/ruamel.yaml">Ruamel.yaml</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Install them using <code>pip install</code> in your virtual environment.</p>
<p>The first one it easier to use but the second one, Ruamel, implements much better the YAML
specification, and allow for example to modify a YAML content without altering comments.</p>
<p>Open a YAML file with:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> ruamel.yaml <span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> YAML

<span class="hljs-keyword">with</span> open(<span class="hljs-string">"filename.yaml"</span>) <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> f:
    yaml=YAML()
    yaml.load(f)
</code></pre>
<h3 id="Anyconfig">Anyconfig</h3>
<p><a href="https://pypi.python.org/pypi/anyconfig">Anyconfig</a> is a very handy package allowing to abstract completely the underlying configuration file format. It allows to load a Python dictionary from JSON, YAML, TOML, and so on.</p>
<p>Install it with:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-bash hljs">pip install anyconfig
</code></pre>
<p>Usage:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> anyconfig

conf1 = anyconfig.load(<span class="hljs-string">"/path/to/foo/conf.d/a.yml"</span>)
</code></pre>
<h2 id="Debugging">Debugging</h2>
<h3 id="Raising-Exceptions">Raising Exceptions</h3>
<p>Exceptions are raised with a raise statement. In code, a raise statement consists of the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>The raise keyword</li>
<li>A call to the Exception() function</li>
<li>A string with a helpful error message passed to the Exception() function</li>
</ul>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">raise</span> Exception(<span class="hljs-string">'This is the error message.'</span>)
Traceback (most recent call last):
  File <span class="hljs-string">"&lt;pyshell#191&gt;"</span>, line <span class="hljs-number">1</span>, <span class="hljs-keyword">in</span> &lt;module&gt;
    <span class="hljs-keyword">raise</span> Exception(<span class="hljs-string">'This is the error message.'</span>)
Exception: This <span class="hljs-keyword">is</span> the error message.
</code></pre>
<p>Often it’s the code that calls the function, not the function itself, that knows how to handle an exception. So you will commonly see a raise statement inside a function and the try and except statements in the code calling the function.</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">box_print</span><span class="hljs-params">(symbol, width, height)</span>:</span>
    <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> len(symbol) != <span class="hljs-number">1</span>:
      <span class="hljs-keyword">raise</span> Exception(<span class="hljs-string">'Symbol must be a single character string.'</span>)
    <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> width &lt;= <span class="hljs-number">2</span>:
      <span class="hljs-keyword">raise</span> Exception(<span class="hljs-string">'Width must be greater than 2.'</span>)
    <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> height &lt;= <span class="hljs-number">2</span>:
      <span class="hljs-keyword">raise</span> Exception(<span class="hljs-string">'Height must be greater than 2.'</span>)
    print(symbol * width)
    <span class="hljs-keyword">for</span> i <span class="hljs-keyword">in</span> range(height - <span class="hljs-number">2</span>):
        print(symbol + (<span class="hljs-string">' '</span> * (width - <span class="hljs-number">2</span>)) + symbol)
    print(symbol * width)
<span class="hljs-keyword">for</span> sym, w, h <span class="hljs-keyword">in</span> ((<span class="hljs-string">'*'</span>, <span class="hljs-number">4</span>, <span class="hljs-number">4</span>), (<span class="hljs-string">'O'</span>, <span class="hljs-number">20</span>, <span class="hljs-number">5</span>), (<span class="hljs-string">'x'</span>, <span class="hljs-number">1</span>, <span class="hljs-number">3</span>), (<span class="hljs-string">'ZZ'</span>, <span class="hljs-number">3</span>, <span class="hljs-number">3</span>)):
    <span class="hljs-keyword">try</span>:
        box_print(sym, w, h)
    <span class="hljs-keyword">except</span> Exception <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> err:
        print(<span class="hljs-string">'An exception happened: '</span> + str(err))
</code></pre>
<h3 id="Getting-the-Traceback-as-a-String">Getting the Traceback as a String</h3>
<p>The traceback is displayed by Python whenever a raised exception goes unhandled. But can also obtain it as a string by calling traceback.format_exc(). This function is useful if you want the information from an exception’s traceback but also want an except statement to gracefully handle the exception. You will need to import Python’s traceback module before calling this function.</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> traceback

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">try</span>:
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>     <span class="hljs-keyword">raise</span> Exception(<span class="hljs-string">'This is the error message.'</span>)
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">except</span>:
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>     <span class="hljs-keyword">with</span> open(<span class="hljs-string">'errorInfo.txt'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'w'</span>) <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> error_file:
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>         error_file.write(traceback.format_exc())
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>     print(<span class="hljs-string">'The traceback info was written to errorInfo.txt.'</span>)
<span class="hljs-number">116</span>
The traceback info was written to errorInfo.txt.
</code></pre>
<p>The 116 is the return value from the write() method, since 116 characters were written to the file. The traceback text was written to errorInfo.txt.</p>
<pre><code class="hljs javascript">Traceback (most recent call last):
  File <span class="hljs-string">"&lt;pyshell#28&gt;"</span>, line <span class="hljs-number">2</span>, <span class="hljs-keyword">in</span> &lt;<span class="hljs-built_in">module</span>&gt;
Exception: This is the error message.
</code></pre>
<h3 id="Assertions">Assertions</h3>
<p>An assertion is a sanity check to make sure your code isn’t doing something obviously wrong. These sanity checks are performed by assert statements. If the sanity check fails, then an AssertionError exception is raised. In code, an assert statement consists of the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>The assert keyword</li>
<li>A condition (that is, an expression that evaluates to True or False)</li>
<li>A comma</li>
<li>A string to display when the condition is False</li>
</ul>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>pod_bay_door_status = <span class="hljs-string">'open'</span>

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">assert</span> pod_bay_door_status == <span class="hljs-string">'open'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'The pod bay doors need to be "open".'</span>

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>pod_bay_door_status = <span class="hljs-string">'I\'m sorry, Dave. I\'m afraid I can\'t do that.'</span>

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">assert</span> pod_bay_door_status == <span class="hljs-string">'open'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'The pod bay doors need to be "open".'</span>

Traceback (most recent call last):
  File <span class="hljs-string">"&lt;pyshell#10&gt;"</span>, line <span class="hljs-number">1</span>, <span class="hljs-keyword">in</span> &lt;module&gt;
    <span class="hljs-keyword">assert</span> pod_bay_door_status == <span class="hljs-string">'open'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'The pod bay doors need to be "open".'</span>
AssertionError: The pod bay doors need to be <span class="hljs-string">"open"</span>.
</code></pre>
<p>In plain English, an assert statement says, “I assert that this condition holds true, and if not, there is a bug somewhere in the program.” Unlike exceptions, your code should not handle assert statements with try and except; if an assert fails, your program should crash. By failing fast like this, you shorten the time between the original cause of the bug and when you first notice the bug. This will reduce the amount of code you will have to check before finding the code that’s causing the bug.</p>
<p>Disabling Assertions</p>
<p>Assertions can be disabled by passing the -O option when running Python.</p>
<h3 id="Logging">Logging</h3>
<p>To enable the logging module to display log messages on your screen as your program runs, copy the following to the top of your program (but under the #! python shebang line):</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> logging

logging.basicConfig(level=logging.DEBUG, format=<span class="hljs-string">' %(asctime)s - %(levelname)s- %(message)s'</span>)
</code></pre>
<p>Say you wrote a function to calculate the factorial of a number. In mathematics, factorial 4 is 1 × 2 × 3 × 4, or 24. Factorial 7 is 1 × 2 × 3 × 4 × 5 × 6 × 7, or 5,040. Open a new file editor window and enter the following code. It has a bug in it, but you will also enter several log messages to help yourself figure out what is going wrong. Save the program as factorialLog.py.</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> logging
&gt;&gt;&gt;
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>logging.basicConfig(level=logging.DEBUG, format=<span class="hljs-string">' %(asctime)s - %(levelname)s- %(message)s'</span>)
&gt;&gt;&gt;
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>logging.debug(<span class="hljs-string">'Start of program'</span>)
&gt;&gt;&gt;
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">factorial</span><span class="hljs-params">(n)</span>:</span>
&gt;&gt;&gt;
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>    logging.debug(<span class="hljs-string">'Start of factorial(%s)'</span> % (n))

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>        total *= i
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>        logging.debug(<span class="hljs-string">'i is '</span> + str(i) + <span class="hljs-string">', total is '</span> + str(total))
&gt;&gt;&gt;
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>    logging.debug(<span class="hljs-string">'End of factorial(%s)'</span> % (n))
&gt;&gt;&gt;
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>    <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> total

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>print(factorial(<span class="hljs-number">5</span>))

<span class="hljs-number">2015</span><span class="hljs-number">-05</span><span class="hljs-number">-23</span> <span class="hljs-number">16</span>:<span class="hljs-number">20</span>:<span class="hljs-number">12</span>,<span class="hljs-number">680</span> - DEBUG - End of factorial(<span class="hljs-number">5</span>)
<span class="hljs-number">0</span>

</code></pre>
<h3 id="Logging-Levels">Logging Levels</h3>
<p>Logging levels provide a way to categorize your log messages by importance. There are five logging levels, described in Table 10-1 from least to most important. Messages can be logged at each level using a different logging function.</p>
<table>
<thead><tr>
<th>Level</th>
<th>Logging Function</th>
<th>Description</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><code>DEBUG</code></td>
<td><code>logging.debug()</code></td>
<td>The lowest level. Used for small details. Usually you care about these messages only when diagnosing problems.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><code>INFO</code></td>
<td><code>logging.info()</code></td>
<td>Used to record information on general events in your program or confirm that things are working at their point in the program.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><code>WARNING</code></td>
<td><code>logging.warning()</code></td>
<td>Used to indicate a potential problem that doesn’t prevent the program from working but might do so in the future.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><code>ERROR</code></td>
<td><code>logging.error()</code></td>
<td>Used to record an error that caused the program to fail to do something.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><code>CRITICAL</code></td>
<td><code>logging.critical()</code></td>
<td>The highest level. Used to indicate a fatal error that has caused or is about to cause the program to stop running entirely.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<h3 id="Disabling-Logging">Disabling Logging</h3>
<p>After you’ve debugged your program, you probably don’t want all these log messages cluttering the screen. The logging.disable() function disables these so that you don’t have to go into your program and remove all the logging calls by hand.</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> logging

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>logging.basicConfig(level=logging.INFO, format=<span class="hljs-string">' %(asctime)s -%(levelname)s - %(message)s'</span>)

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>logging.critical(<span class="hljs-string">'Critical error! Critical error!'</span>)
<span class="hljs-number">2015</span><span class="hljs-number">-05</span><span class="hljs-number">-22</span> <span class="hljs-number">11</span>:<span class="hljs-number">10</span>:<span class="hljs-number">48</span>,<span class="hljs-number">054</span> - CRITICAL - Critical error! Critical error!

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>logging.disable(logging.CRITICAL)

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>logging.critical(<span class="hljs-string">'Critical error! Critical error!'</span>)

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>logging.error(<span class="hljs-string">'Error! Error!'</span>)
</code></pre>
<h3 id="Logging-to-a-File">Logging to a File</h3>
<p>Instead of displaying the log messages to the screen, you can write them to a text file. The logging.basicConfig() function takes a filename keyword argument, like so:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> logging

logging.basicConfig(filename=<span class="hljs-string">'myProgramLog.txt'</span>, level=logging.DEBUG, format=<span class="hljs-string">'%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s'</span>)
</code></pre>
<h2 id="Lambda-Functions">Lambda Functions</h2>
<p>This function:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">add</span><span class="hljs-params">(x, y)</span>:</span>
        <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> x + y

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>add(<span class="hljs-number">5</span>, <span class="hljs-number">3</span>)
<span class="hljs-number">8</span>
</code></pre>
<p>Is equivalent to the <em>lambda</em> function:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>add = <span class="hljs-keyword">lambda</span> x, y: x + y
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>add(<span class="hljs-number">5</span>, <span class="hljs-number">3</span>)
<span class="hljs-number">8</span>
</code></pre>
<p>It's not even need to bind it to a name like add before:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>(<span class="hljs-keyword">lambda</span> x, y: x + y)(<span class="hljs-number">5</span>, <span class="hljs-number">3</span>)
<span class="hljs-number">8</span>
</code></pre>
<p>Like regular nested functions, lambdas also work as lexical closures:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">make_adder</span><span class="hljs-params">(n)</span>:</span>
        <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">lambda</span> x: x + n

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>plus_3 = make_adder(<span class="hljs-number">3</span>)
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>plus_5 = make_adder(<span class="hljs-number">5</span>)

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>plus_3(<span class="hljs-number">4</span>)
<span class="hljs-number">7</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>plus_5(<span class="hljs-number">4</span>)
<span class="hljs-number">9</span>
</code></pre>
<p>Note: lambda can only evaluate an expression, like a single line of code.</p>
<h2 id="Ternary-Conditional-Operator">Ternary Conditional Operator</h2>
<p>Many programming languages have a ternary operator, which define a conditional expression. The most common usage is to make a terse simple conditional assignment statement. In other words, it offers one-line code to evaluate the first expression if the condition is true, otherwise it evaluates the second expression.</p>
<pre><code class="hljs xml"><span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">expression1</span>&gt;</span> if <span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">condition</span>&gt;</span> else <span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">expression2</span>&gt;</span>
</code></pre>
<p>Example:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>age = <span class="hljs-number">15</span>

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>print(<span class="hljs-string">'kid'</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> age &lt; <span class="hljs-number">18</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">else</span> <span class="hljs-string">'adult'</span>)
kid
</code></pre>
<p>Ternary operators can be chained:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>age = <span class="hljs-number">15</span>

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>print(<span class="hljs-string">'kid'</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> age &lt; <span class="hljs-number">13</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">else</span> <span class="hljs-string">'teenager'</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> age &lt; <span class="hljs-number">18</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">else</span> <span class="hljs-string">'adult'</span>)
teenager
</code></pre>
<p>The code above is equivalent to:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> age &lt; <span class="hljs-number">18</span>:
    <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> age &lt; <span class="hljs-number">13</span>:
        print(<span class="hljs-string">'kid'</span>)
    <span class="hljs-keyword">else</span>:
        print(<span class="hljs-string">'teenager'</span>)
<span class="hljs-keyword">else</span>:
    print(<span class="hljs-string">'adult'</span>)
</code></pre>
<h2 id="args-and-kwargs">args and kwargs</h2>
<p>The names <code>args and kwargs</code> are arbitrary - the important thing are the <code>*</code> and <code>**</code> operators. They can mean:</p>
<ol>
<li><p>In a function declaration, <code>*</code> means “pack all remaining positional arguments into a tuple named <code>&lt;name&gt;</code>”, while <code>**</code> is the same for keyword arguments (except it uses a dictionary, not a tuple).</p>
</li>
<li><p>In a function call, <code>*</code> means “unpack tuple or list named <code>&lt;name&gt;</code> to positional arguments at this position”, while <code>**</code> is the same for keyword arguments.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>For example you can make a function that you can use to call any other function, no matter what parameters it has:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">forward</span><span class="hljs-params">(f, *args, **kwargs)</span>:</span>
    <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> f(*args, **kwargs)
</code></pre>
<p>Inside forward, args is a tuple (of all positional arguments except the first one, because we specified it - the f), kwargs is a dict. Then we call f and unpack them so they become normal arguments to f.</p>
<p>You use <code>*args</code> when you have an indefinite amount of positional arguments.</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">fruits</span><span class="hljs-params">(*args)</span>:</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>   <span class="hljs-keyword">for</span> fruit <span class="hljs-keyword">in</span> args:
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>      print(fruit)

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>fruits(<span class="hljs-string">"apples"</span>, <span class="hljs-string">"bananas"</span>, <span class="hljs-string">"grapes"</span>)

<span class="hljs-string">"apples"</span>
<span class="hljs-string">"bananas"</span>
<span class="hljs-string">"grapes"</span>
</code></pre>
<p>Similarly, you use <code>**kwargs</code> when you have an indefinite number of keyword arguments.</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">fruit</span><span class="hljs-params">(**kwargs)</span>:</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>   <span class="hljs-keyword">for</span> key, value <span class="hljs-keyword">in</span> kwargs.items():
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>       print(<span class="hljs-string">"{0}: {1}"</span>.format(key, value))

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>fruit(name = <span class="hljs-string">"apple"</span>, color = <span class="hljs-string">"red"</span>)

name: apple
color: red
</code></pre>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">show</span><span class="hljs-params">(arg1, arg2, *args, kwarg1=None, kwarg2=None, **kwargs)</span>:</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>  print(arg1)
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>  print(arg2)
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>  print(args)
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>  print(kwarg1)
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>  print(kwarg2)
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>  print(kwargs)

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>data1 = [<span class="hljs-number">1</span>,<span class="hljs-number">2</span>,<span class="hljs-number">3</span>]
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>data2 = [<span class="hljs-number">4</span>,<span class="hljs-number">5</span>,<span class="hljs-number">6</span>]
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>data3 = {<span class="hljs-string">'a'</span>:<span class="hljs-number">7</span>,<span class="hljs-string">'b'</span>:<span class="hljs-number">8</span>,<span class="hljs-string">'c'</span>:<span class="hljs-number">9</span>}

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>show(*data1,*data2, kwarg1=<span class="hljs-string">"python"</span>,kwarg2=<span class="hljs-string">"cheatsheet"</span>,**data3)
<span class="hljs-number">1</span>
<span class="hljs-number">2</span>
(<span class="hljs-number">3</span>, <span class="hljs-number">4</span>, <span class="hljs-number">5</span>, <span class="hljs-number">6</span>)
python
cheatsheet
{<span class="hljs-string">'a'</span>: <span class="hljs-number">7</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'b'</span>: <span class="hljs-number">8</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'c'</span>: <span class="hljs-number">9</span>}

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>show(*data1, *data2, **data3)
<span class="hljs-number">1</span>
<span class="hljs-number">2</span>
(<span class="hljs-number">3</span>, <span class="hljs-number">4</span>, <span class="hljs-number">5</span>, <span class="hljs-number">6</span>)
<span class="hljs-literal">None</span>
<span class="hljs-literal">None</span>
{<span class="hljs-string">'a'</span>: <span class="hljs-number">7</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'b'</span>: <span class="hljs-number">8</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'c'</span>: <span class="hljs-number">9</span>}

<span class="hljs-comment"># If you do not specify ** for kwargs</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>show(*data1, *data2, *data3)
<span class="hljs-number">1</span>
<span class="hljs-number">2</span>
(<span class="hljs-number">3</span>, <span class="hljs-number">4</span>, <span class="hljs-number">5</span>, <span class="hljs-number">6</span>, <span class="hljs-string">"a"</span>, <span class="hljs-string">"b"</span>, <span class="hljs-string">"c"</span>)
<span class="hljs-literal">None</span>
<span class="hljs-literal">None</span>
{}
</code></pre>
<h3 id="Things-to-Remember(args)">Things to Remember(args)</h3>
<ol>
<li>Functions can accept a variable number of positional arguments by using <code>*args</code> in the def statement.</li>
<li>You can use the items from a sequence as the positional arguments for a function with the <code>*</code> operator.</li>
<li>Using the <code>*</code> operator with a generator may cause your program to run out of memory and crash.</li>
<li>Adding new positional parameters to functions that accept <code>*args</code> can introduce hard-to-find bugs.</li>
</ol>
<h3 id="Things-to-Remember(kwargs)">Things to Remember(kwargs)</h3>
<ol>
<li>Function arguments can be specified by position or by keyword.</li>
<li>Keywords make it clear what the purpose of each argument is when it would be confusing with only positional arguments.</li>
<li>Keyword arguments with default values make it easy to add new behaviors to a function, especially when the function has existing callers.</li>
<li>Optional keyword arguments should always be passed by keyword instead of by position.</li>
</ol>
<h2 id="Context-Manager">Context Manager</h2>
<p>While Python's context managers are widely used, few understand the purpose behind their use. These statements, commonly used with reading and writing files, assist the application in conserving system memory and improve resource management by ensuring specific resources are only in use for certain processes.</p>
<h3 id="with-statement">with statement</h3>
<p>A context manager is an object that is notified when a context (a block of code) starts and ends. You commonly use one with the with statement. It takes care of the notifying.</p>
<p>For example, file objects are context managers. When a context ends, the file object is closed automatically:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">with</span> open(filename) <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> f:
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>    file_contents = f.read()

<span class="hljs-comment"># the open_file object has automatically been closed.</span>
</code></pre>
<p>Anything that ends execution of the block causes the context manager's exit method to be called. This includes exceptions, and can be useful when an error causes you to prematurely exit from an open file or connection. Exiting a script without properly closing files/connections is a bad idea, that may cause data loss or other problems. By using a context manager you can ensure that precautions are always taken to prevent damage or loss in this way.</p>
<h3 id="Writing-your-own-contextmanager-using-generator-syntax">Writing your own contextmanager using generator syntax</h3>
<p>It is also possible to write a context manager using generator syntax thanks to the <code>contextlib.contextmanager</code> decorator:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> contextlib
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>@contextlib.contextmanager
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span><span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">context_manager</span><span class="hljs-params">(num)</span>:</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    print(<span class="hljs-string">'Enter'</span>)
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    <span class="hljs-keyword">yield</span> num + <span class="hljs-number">1</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    print(<span class="hljs-string">'Exit'</span>)
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">with</span> context_manager(<span class="hljs-number">2</span>) <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> cm:
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    <span class="hljs-comment"># the following instructions are run when the 'yield' point of the context</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    <span class="hljs-comment"># manager is reached.</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    <span class="hljs-comment"># 'cm' will have the value that was yielded</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    print(<span class="hljs-string">'Right in the middle with cm = {}'</span>.format(cm))
Enter
Right <span class="hljs-keyword">in</span> the middle <span class="hljs-keyword">with</span> cm = <span class="hljs-number">3</span>
Exit

&gt;&gt;&gt;
</code></pre>
<h2 id="__main__-Top-level-script-environment"><code>__main__</code> Top-level script environment</h2>
<p><code>__main__</code> is the name of the scope in which top-level code executes.
A module’s <strong>name</strong> is set equal to <code>__main__</code> when read from standard input, a script, or from an interactive prompt.</p>
<p>A module can discover whether or not it is running in the main scope by checking its own <code>__name__</code>, which allows a common idiom for conditionally executing code in a module when it is run as a script or with <code>python -m</code> but not when it is imported:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> __name__ == <span class="hljs-string">"__main__"</span>:
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    <span class="hljs-comment"># execute only if run as a script</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    main()
</code></pre>
<p>For a package, the same effect can be achieved by including a <strong>main</strong>.py module, the contents of which will be executed when the module is run with -m</p>
<p>For example we are developing script which is designed to be used as module, we should do:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-comment"># Python program to execute function directly</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">add</span><span class="hljs-params">(a, b)</span>:</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> a+b
...
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>add(<span class="hljs-number">10</span>, <span class="hljs-number">20</span>) <span class="hljs-comment"># we can test it by calling the function save it as calculate.py</span>
<span class="hljs-number">30</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-comment"># Now if we want to use that module by importing we have to comment out our call,</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-comment"># Instead we can write like this in calculate.py</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> __name__ == <span class="hljs-string">"__main__"</span>:
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    add(<span class="hljs-number">3</span>, <span class="hljs-number">5</span>)
...
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> calculate
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>calculate.add(<span class="hljs-number">3</span>, <span class="hljs-number">5</span>)
<span class="hljs-number">8</span>
</code></pre>
<h3 id="Advantages">Advantages</h3>
<ol>
<li>Every Python module has it’s <code>__name__</code> defined and if this is <code>__main__</code>, it implies that the module is being run standalone by the user and we can do corresponding appropriate actions.</li>
<li>If you import this script as a module in another script, the <strong>name</strong> is set to the name of the script/module.</li>
<li>Python files can act as either reusable modules, or as standalone programs.</li>
<li>if <code>__name__ == “main”:</code> is used to execute some code only if the file was run directly, and not imported.</li>
</ol>
<h2 id="setup.py">setup.py</h2>
<p>The setup script is the centre of all activity in building, distributing, and installing modules using the Distutils. The main purpose of the setup script is to describe your module distribution to the Distutils, so that the various commands that operate on your modules do the right thing.</p>
<p>The <code>setup.py</code> file is at the heart of a Python project. It describes all of the metadata about your project. There a quite a few fields you can add to a project to give it a rich set of metadata describing the project. However, there are only three required fields: name, version, and packages. The name field must be unique if you wish to publish your package on the Python Package Index (PyPI). The version field keeps track of different releases of the project. The packages field describes where you’ve put the Python source code within your project.</p>
<p>This allows you to easily install Python packages. Often it's enough to write:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-bash hljs">python setup.py install
</code></pre>
<p>and module will install itself.</p>
<p>Our initial setup.py will also include information about the license and will re-use the README.txt file for the long_description field. This will look like:</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> distutils.core <span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> setup
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>setup(
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>   name=<span class="hljs-string">'pythonCheatsheet'</span>,
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>   version=<span class="hljs-string">'0.1'</span>,
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>   packages=[<span class="hljs-string">'pipenv'</span>,],
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>   license=<span class="hljs-string">'MIT'</span>,
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>   long_description=open(<span class="hljs-string">'README.txt'</span>).read(),
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>)
</code></pre>
<p>Find more information visit <a href="http://docs.python.org/install/index.html">http://docs.python.org/install/index.html</a>.</p>
<h2 id="Dataclasses">Dataclasses</h2>
<p><code>Dataclasses</code> are python classes but are suited for storing data objects.
This module provides a decorator and functions for automatically adding generated special methods such as <code>__init__()</code> and <code>__repr__()</code> to user-defined classes.</p>
<h3 id="Features">Features</h3>
<ol>
<li><p>They store data and represent a certain data type. Ex: A number. For people familiar with ORMs, a model instance is a data object. It represents a specific kind of entity. It holds attributes that define or represent the entity.</p>
</li>
<li><p>They can be compared to other objects of the same type. Ex: A number can be greater than, less than, or equal to another number.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Python 3.7 provides a decorator dataclass that is used to convert a class into a dataclass.</p>
<p>python 2.7</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">Number</span>:</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">def</span> <span class="hljs-title">__init__</span><span class="hljs-params">(self, val)</span>:</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>        self.val = val
...
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>obj = Number(<span class="hljs-number">2</span>)
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>obj.val
<span class="hljs-number">2</span>
</code></pre>
<p>with dataclass</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>@dataclass
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span><span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">Number</span>:</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    val: int
...
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>obj = Number(<span class="hljs-number">2</span>)
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>obj.val
<span class="hljs-number">2</span>
</code></pre>
<h3 id="Default-values">Default values</h3>
<p>It is easy to add default values to the fields of your data class.</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>@dataclass
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span><span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">Product</span>:</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    name: str
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    count: int = <span class="hljs-number">0</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>    price: float = <span class="hljs-number">0.0</span>
...
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>obj = Product(<span class="hljs-string">"Python"</span>)
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>obj.name
Python
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>obj.count
<span class="hljs-number">0</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>obj.price
<span class="hljs-number">0.0</span>
</code></pre>
<h3 id="Type-hints">Type hints</h3>
<p>It is mandatory to define the data type in dataclass. However, If you don't want specify the datatype then, use <code>typing.Any</code>.</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python hljs"><span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> dataclasses <span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> dataclass
<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span><span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> typing <span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> Any

<span class="hljs-meta">&gt;&gt;&gt; </span>@dataclass
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span><span class="hljs-class"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">WithoutExplicitTypes</span>:</span>
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>   name: Any
<span class="hljs-meta">... </span>   value: Any = <span class="hljs-number">42</span>
...
</code></pre>
<h2 id="Virtual-Environment">Virtual Environment</h2>
<p>The use of a Virtual Environment is to test python code in encapsulated environments and to also avoid filling the base Python installation with libraries we might use for only one project.</p>
<h3 id="virtualenv">virtualenv</h3>
<ol>
<li><p>Install virtualenv</p>
<pre><code class="hljs">pip install virtualenv
</code></pre>
</li>
<li><p>Install virtualenvwrapper-win (Windows)</p>
<pre><code class="hljs">pip install virtualenvwrapper-win
</code></pre>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Usage:</p>
<ol>
<li><p>Make a Virtual Environment</p>
<pre><code class="hljs">mkvirtualenv HelloWold
</code></pre>
<p>Anything we install now will be specific to this project. And available to the projects we connect to this environment.</p>
</li>
<li><p>Set Project Directory</p>
<p>To bind our virtualenv with our current working directory we simply enter:</p>
<pre><code class="hljs">setprojectdir .
</code></pre>
</li>
<li><p>Deactivate</p>
<p>To move onto something else in the command line type ‘deactivate’ to deactivate your environment.</p>
<pre><code class="hljs">deactivate
</code></pre>
<p>Notice how the parenthesis disappear.</p>
</li>
<li><p>Workon</p>
<p>Open up the command prompt and type ‘workon HelloWold’ to activate the environment and move into your root project folder</p>
<pre><code class="hljs">workon HelloWold
</code></pre>
</li>
</ol>
<h3 id="poetry">poetry</h3>
<blockquote><p><a href="https://poetry.eustace.io/">Poetry</a> is a tool for dependency management and packaging in Python. It allows you to declare the libraries your project depends on and it will manage (install/update) them for you.</p>
</blockquote>
<ol>
<li><p>Install Poetry</p>
<pre><code class="hljs">pip install --user poetry
</code></pre>
</li>
<li><p>Create a new project</p>
<pre><code class="hljs javascript">poetry <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> my-project
</code></pre>
<p>This will create a my-project directory:</p>
<pre><code class="hljs markdown">my-project
├── pyproject.toml
├── README.rst
├── poetry_demo
│   └── <span class="hljs-strong">__init__</span>.py
└── tests
<span class="hljs-code">    ├── __init__.py</span>
<span class="hljs-code">    └── test_poetry_demo.py</span>
</code></pre>
<p>The pyproject.toml file will orchestrate your project and its dependencies:</p>
<pre><code class="hljs bash">[tool.poetry]
name = <span class="hljs-string">"my-project"</span>
version = <span class="hljs-string">"0.1.0"</span>
description = <span class="hljs-string">""</span>
authors = [<span class="hljs-string">"your name &lt;your@mail.com&gt;"</span>]

[tool.poetry.dependencies]
python = <span class="hljs-string">"*"</span>

[tool.poetry.dev-dependencies]
pytest = <span class="hljs-string">"^3.4"</span>
</code></pre>
</li>
<li><p>Packages</p>
<p>To add dependencies to your project, you can specify them in the tool.poetry.dependencies section:</p>
<pre><code class="hljs bash">[tool.poetry.dependencies]
pendulum = <span class="hljs-string">"^1.4"</span>
</code></pre>
<p>Also, instead of modifying the pyproject.toml file by hand, you can use the add command and it will automatically find a suitable version constraint.</p>
<pre><code class="hljs">$ poetry add pendulum
</code></pre>
<p>To install the dependencies listed in the pyproject.toml:</p>
<pre><code class="hljs">poetry install
</code></pre>
<p>To remove dependencies:</p>
<pre><code class="hljs">poetry remove pendulum
</code></pre>
</li>
</ol>
<p>For more information, check the <a href="https://poetry.eustace.io/docs/">documentation</a>.</p>
<h3 id="pipenv">pipenv</h3>
<blockquote><p><a href="https://pipenv.readthedocs.io/en/latest/">Pipenv</a> is a tool that aims to bring the best of all packaging worlds (bundler, composer, npm, cargo, yarn, etc.) to the Python world. Windows is a first-class citizen, in our world.</p>
</blockquote>
<ol>
<li><p>Install pipenv</p>
<pre><code class="hljs">pip install pipenv
</code></pre>
</li>
<li><p>Enter your Project directory and install the Packages for your project</p>
<pre><code class="hljs bash"><span class="hljs-built_in">cd</span> my_project
pipenv install &lt;package&gt;
</code></pre>
<p>Pipenv will install your package and create a Pipfile for you in your project’s directory. The Pipfile is used to track which dependencies your project needs in case you need to re-install them.</p>
</li>
<li><p>Uninstall Packages</p>
<pre><code class="hljs xml">pipenv uninstall <span class="hljs-tag">&lt;<span class="hljs-name">package</span>&gt;</span>
</code></pre>
</li>
<li><p>Activate the Virtual Environment associated with your Python project</p>
<pre><code class="hljs">pipenv shell
</code></pre>
</li>
<li><p>Exit the Virtual Environment</p>
<pre><code class="hljs bash"><span class="hljs-built_in">exit</span>
</code></pre>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Find more information and a video in <a href="https://docs.pipenv.org/">docs.pipenv.org</a>.</p>
<h3 id="anaconda">anaconda</h3>
<p><a href="https://anaconda.org/">Anaconda</a> is another popular tool to manage python packages.</p>
<blockquote><p>Where packages, notebooks, projects and environments are shared.
Your place for free public conda package hosting.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Usage:</p>
<ol>
<li><p>Make a Virtual Environment</p>
<pre><code class="hljs">conda create -n HelloWorld
</code></pre>
</li>
<li><p>To use the Virtual Environment, activate it by:</p>
<pre><code class="hljs">conda activate HelloWorld
</code></pre>
<p>Anything installed now will be specific to the project HelloWorld</p>
</li>
<li><p>Exit the Virtual Environment</p>
<pre><code class="hljs">conda deactivate
</code></pre>
</li>
</ol>

      </div>
    </div>
  </div>
</div>
